## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through a constitutive law and temperature modifies material properties through thermal softening or stiffening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon (Hooke's law at fixed temperature)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 + c2 * T) * epsilon (linear T-dependence of modulus)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (Hollomon + linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal dependence)
- Power-law hardening with exponential softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (combined nonlinear hardening and exponential thermal effect)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce-type saturation: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with T-dependence)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (polynomial constitutive law)
- Ludwik model with thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik hardening + Arrhenius softening)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Cross-term model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (linear model with strain-temperature coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Stress-strain slope (elastic modulus) is a function of T, often linear or exponential in T
- Strain hardening saturation → Stress increases with strain but saturates, suggesting (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or epsilon**c with c<1
- Thermal softening → Multiplicative factor that decreases with temperature: (1 - c*T**m) or exp(-c*T)
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (T - T_ref) or (T / T_melt) in normalized form, i.e., (c0 - c1*T)
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T indicate that hardening rate changes with temperature
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield stress before hardening: (c0 + f(epsilon))
- Thermally-activated deformation → Arrhenius-type exp(c0 / T) terms for diffusion-controlled or creep-like behavior
- Elastic-plastic transition → Piecewise or smooth transition near yield point, modeled by sqrt(epsilon**2 + c) or similar regularization
